**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The crisis is so profound that one headline claims Jeffrey Epstein has, "From the Grave," succeeded in shutting down the House [4]. The combined effect has been to "Totally Derailed" both the House and the Executive Branch, halting normal government function [5]. In response to this maneuver, Democrats have signaled their intent to "play hardball on Epstein files," indicating that this conflict will escalate further upon Congress's return [6].

This is compounded by significant upheaval within the Department of Justice, a direct and public war of words between the current and former Presidents, and the implementation of impactful new domestic and foreign policy directives. The political and operational environment is extremely volatile, marked by institutional paralysis, executive assertiveness, and deepening partisan divides. All personnel should be aware of the high potential for further instability.

---
**Area 1: The Epstein Documents Crisis and Government Disruption**

**Topic 1.1: Congress Adjourns Amid Crisis Over Epstein Files**

The legislative branch is in a state of paralysis, directly attributed to the controversy surrounding the Jeffrey Epstein files. House Speaker Mike Johnson has shut down Congress for the summer, an action multiple outlets report was executed specifically to prevent a vote on the release of the files and to avoid a confrontation over President Trump's handling of the matter [1, 2]. This has led to a situation where the House has effectively "fled Washington" [3]. The crisis is so profound that one headline claims Jeffrey Epstein has, "From the Grave," succeeded in shutting down the House [4]. The combined effect has been to "Totally Derailed" both the House and the Executive Branch, halting normal government function [5]. In response to this maneuver, Democrats have signaled their intent to "play hardball on Epstein files," indicating that this conflict will escalate further upon Congress's return [6].

**Topic 1.2: Judicial and Congressional Investigations Intensify**

Legal and congressional pressure is mounting from multiple directions. The judiciary has ordered the Trump administration to produce "Epstein Transcripts" complete with proposed redactions for review [1]. However, in a subsequent and significant setback for the administration, judges ruled that its motions to unseal the grand jury transcripts for both Epstein and Ghislaine Maxwell were "inadequate" [2]. In a parallel track, the House Oversight Committee has announced that it will issue a subpoena to Ghislaine Maxwell, according to a spokesperson [3]. Adding another layer of intrigue, a separate headline alludes to the potential existence of "secret recordings that could blow open Trump’s true relationship with Epstein," though the specific contents and whereabouts of these alleged recordings are not detailed [4].

The White House is engaged in active political management of the crisis, with reports suggesting a strategy of distraction. The White House is engaged in active political management of the crisis, with reports suggesting a strategy of distraction. President Trump is allegedly using the release of files pertaining to Martin Luther King Jr. as a diversion, while also launching attacks against former President Obama, in what is described as an overt attempt to shift the media narrative away from the Epstein fallout [1, 2]. The administration was also forced to issue a formal reaction to a separate report alleging that the FBI had been asked to specifically flag any mention of President Trump in the Epstein files [3]. Despite these efforts, critics assert the President is "marooned on Epstein’s island" [4] and is only "fuel[ing] the Epstein furor he wants to escape" [5] by continuing to evade questions about his associates, whom another headline explicitly refers to as his "Child Sex Trafficking Friends" [6].

[1] How Trump is using MLK and Obama to distract from Epstein files, https://www.thetimes.com/us/american-politics/article/how-trump-is-using-mlk-and-obama-to-distract-from-epstein-files-kzsgmbc6d  
[2] Trump targets Obama in attempt to distract from Epstein files fallout, https://www.msnbc.com/katy-tur/watch/trump-targets-obama-in-attempt-to-distract-from-epstein-files-fallout-243651141643

## 2. Justice Department and Legal System Developments

### 2.1. Judicial Standoff Over New Jersey U.S. Attorney's Office

A significant conflict has erupted between the federal judiciary and the Department of Justice over the leadership of the New Jersey U.S. Attorney's Office. In an extraordinary move, federal judges in the state acted to "oust" or "bench" Trump ally Alina Habba from her role as the state’s top federal prosecutor [1, 2]. The DOJ, led by Attorney General Pam Bondi, responded immediately and forcefully. Bondi announced that the prosecutor the judges had selected to succeed Habba was removed from the position [3]. A Fox News report characterizes the move as the DOJ "swiftly fir[ing] Alina Habba's court-appointed replacement," highlighting the escalating nature of the inter-branch dispute [4].

**References:**
[1] Judges oust Trump ally Alina Habba as New Jersey’s top prosecutor, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/07/22/judges-decline-to-keep-alina-habba-new-jersey-top-prosecutor-00467976  
[2] New Jersey federal judges bench Alina Habba as U.S. attorney, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/alina-habba-new-jersey-judges-block-nomination/  
[3] Pam Bondi says judge-picked New Jersey prosecutor succeeding Alina Habba has been removed, https://apnews.com/article/new-jersey-us-attorney-prosecutor-habba-trump-63ffc37d0c7afe5ba431b5b414a7eb92

### 2.2. Shake-up at Department of Justice Headquarters

In a notable personnel change within the Department of Justice leadership, Attorney General Pam Bondi has fired the department's top ethics adviser [1]. The move is reported under a "Trump administration" tag by The Guardian, underscoring its political significance.

## 3. Executive Branch and Presidential Actions

### 3.1. President Trump Accuses Former President Obama of "Treason"

President Trump has escalated his political attacks by publicly accusing former President Barack Obama of "treason" in remarks made directly from the Oval Office [1]. This prompted a rare and direct rebuke from the former President's office, which issued a statement calling the claims "bizarre," "ridiculous," and a "weak attempt at distraction" [2, 3]. In its response, Obama's office strategically reiterated the intelligence community's conclusion of attempted Russian interference in the 2016 election, a pointed comeback to what one outlet described as Trump's "Russia 'treason' threats" [4, 5].

### 3.2. Presidential Statements on Media and Foreign Policy

President Trump has made several public statements regarding media organizations and figures. He called for the firing of late-night hosts Jimmy Kimmel and Jimmy Fallon [1]. He also claimed the new owner of CBS would provide him with $20 million in airtime following a settlement and touted a "Secret Paramount Side Deal After Colbert Ouster" [2, 3]. In foreign policy, the administration has formally withdrawn the United States from UNESCO, the UN's culture and education agency [4]. Finally, the administration has had to contend with a misinformation campaign, after a fake resignation letter from Fed Chair Jerome Powell duped allies like Senator Mike Lee [5].

## 4. Domestic Policy, Agency Actions, and Social Issues

### 4.1. Economic Fallout from Tariffs and Trade Disputes

The administration's trade policies are facing increased scrutiny due to their tangible economic consequences. General Motors has publicly stated that President Trump's tariffs resulted in a $1.1 billion negative impact on its operating income in the last quarter alone [1]. Concurrently, a trade war with Canada has reportedly led to a 66% plunge in U.S. alcohol sales to the country, with one headline stating that Canada "kicks American booze" in retaliation [2]. Democrats are reportedly seizing on this issue, using the tariffs to "turn inflation on Trump" [3].

**References:**

### 4.2. Implementation of New Social and Cultural Policies

The administration is moving forward with policies affecting the LGBTQ+ community. An internal military memo, obtained by 404 Media, reveals that bathrooms will be "'Continuously' Monitor[ed]" to ensure compliance with a new anti-trans order. The same memo shows the military also ordered a review of "questionable content" at the editorially independent Stars and Stripes newspaper [1]. In a related development, the U.S. Olympic & Paralympic Committee has confirmed it will comply with President Trump's ban on the participation of transgender women in women’s sports [2].

Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) actions continue to draw public criticism. In one case, rights groups allege an Atlanta-based reporter was detained by ICE as punishment for his journalism [1]. In another, a deaf and mute DACA recipient was arrested and shipped to Texas [2]. ## 5. Party Politics and Electoral Dynamics

### 5.1. Partisan Battle Over Texas Redistricting

A major political battle is escalating in the Texas state legislature over congressional redistricting. In a direct challenge to the Republican majority's effort to pass a new map, Texas Democrats have vowed to employ a range of delay tactics. With few procedural options available to block the map outright, Democrats have threatened actions including filibusters, delaying hearings, and, most significantly, breaking quorum to halt the legislative process [1].

**References:**
[1] Texas Democrats vow to use delay tactics to drag out GOP redistricting effort; With few options to prevent the Republican majority from passing a new congressional map, Democrats threatened to filibuster, delay hearings and even break quorum., https://www.texastribune.org/2025/07/21/texas-democrats-redistricting-special-session-delay-quorum-break/  

### 5.2. Democratic Party Navigates Internal Divisions

The Democratic party is confronting significant internal divisions and strategic challenges. A Politico report suggests the party has been "bleeding working-class support," a trend exacerbated by the fact that some potential 2028 presidential contenders are now "fighting with unions" [1]. Divisive foreign policy issues are also creating friction. Rep. Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez reportedly received death threats after her office was vandalized, an act attributed in the headline to "anti-Israel supporters" [2]. In New York politics, the mayoral candidacy of Zohran Mamdani is highlighting party rifts after Israeli Prime Minister Netanyahu spoke out against him for pledging to uphold an ICC arrest warrant [3].

**References:**
[1] Dems have been bleeding working-class support. Now possible 2028 contenders are fighting with unions., https://www.politico.com/news/2025/07/22/unions-labor-feuds-democratic-governors-2028-00465117

## 6. Congressional Activities and Legislation

### 6.1. Funding Clawbacks and Kennedy Center Renaming

A recent decision by Congress to approve funding clawbacks is causing significant distress for public broadcasters. According to a Politico report, "frustration and fear" are rippling through NPR and PBS affiliates nationwide as a consequence of the approved measure [1]. Separately, another legislative effort is drawing attention as House Republicans advance a proposal to rename the Kennedy Center Opera House in honor of former First Lady Melania Trump [2, 3]. A USA Today report states that lawmakers have already voted on the measure [4], a move Democrats allege the GOP "'snuck in'" without proper process [5].
